<li>
<section class="detail" id="lpNorm(int)">
<h3>lpNorm</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">double</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">lpNorm</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(int&nbsp;p)</span></div>
<div class="block">Computes the lp-norm of the matrix.
 <p>
 The lp-norm, also known as the L^p norm, is a measure of the magnitude of the
 matrix. It is calculated by summing the absolute values of the matrix
 elements raised to the power of p, and then taking the p-th root of the sum.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 double norm = matrix.lpNorm(2); // Computes the L^2 norm (Euclidean norm)
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>p</code> - the order of the norm (p >= 1)</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>the lp-norm</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="l1Norm()">
<h3>l1Norm</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">double</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">l1Norm</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Computes the l1-norm (Manhattan norm) of the matrix.
 <p>
 The l1-norm is a measure of the magnitude of the matrix, calculated as the
 sum of the absolute values of its elements.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 double norm = matrix.l1Norm(); // Computes the L^1 norm (Manhattan norm)
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>the l1-norm</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="l2Norm()">
<h3>l2Norm</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">double</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">l2Norm</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Computes the l2-norm (Euclidean norm) of the matrix.
 <p>
 The l2-norm is a measure of the magnitude of the matrix, calculated as the
 square root of the sum of the squares of its elements.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 double norm = matrix.l2Norm(); // Computes the L^2 norm (Euclidean norm)
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>the l2-norm</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="infinityNorm()">
<h3>infinityNorm</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">double</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">infinityNorm</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Computes the infinity-norm of the matrix.
 <p>
 The infinity-norm is the maximum absolute value of the elements in the
 matrix. It is a measure of the magnitude of the matrix.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 double norm = matrix.infinityNorm(); // Computes the infinity-norm
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>the infinity-norm</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="frobeniusNorm()">
<h3>frobeniusNorm</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">double</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">frobeniusNorm</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Computes the Frobenius norm of the matrix.
 <p>
 The Frobenius norm is the square root of the sum of the squares of the
 elements of the matrix. It is a measure of the magnitude of the matrix.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 double norm = matrix.frobeniusNorm(); // Computes the Frobenius norm
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>the Frobenius norm</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="pq_norm(int,int)">
<h3>pq_norm</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">double</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">pq_norm</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(int&nbsp;p,
 int&nbsp;q)</span></div>
<div class="block">Computes the pq-norm of the matrix.
 <p>
 The pq-norm is a generalization of the lp-norm, where the matrix is first
 transformed into a p-norm along the columns, and then the q-norm of the
 transformed matrix is calculated.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 double norm = matrix.pq_norm(2, 2); // Computes the 2,2-norm
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>p</code> - the order of the norm along the columns (p >= 1)</dd>
<dd><code>q</code> - the order of the norm of the transformed matrix (q >= 1)</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>the pq-norm</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="maxAbsValue()">
<h3>maxAbsValue</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">double</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">maxAbsValue</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Computes the maximum absolute value of the matrix.
 <p>
 This method finds the maximum absolute value among all the elements of the
 matrix.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 double maxAbs = matrix.maxAbsValue(); // Finds the maximum absolute value in the matrix
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>the maximum absolute value</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="kyFanNorm(int)">
<h3>kyFanNorm</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">double</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">kyFanNorm</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(int&nbsp;k)</span>
                 throws <span class="exceptions"><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></span></div>
<div class="block">Calculates the Ky Fan k-norm of the matrix.
 <p>
 The Ky Fan k-norm is the sum of the k largest singular values of the matrix.
 It is a measure of the matrix's "spread" or "width" in its singular value
 decomposition.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 double kyFanNorm = matrix.kyFanNorm(2); // Computes the 2-norm of the matrix's singular values
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>k</code> - The number of largest singular values to sum.</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The Ky Fan k-norm of the matrix.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if k is less than 1 or greater than the
                                  number of singular values.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="trace()">
<h3>trace</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">double</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">trace</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Computes the trace of the matrix.
 <p>
 The trace of a matrix is the sum of the elements on its main diagonal. It is
 a measure of the matrix's "identity" or "self".
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 double trace = matrix.trace(); // Computes the trace of the matrix
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>the trace of the matrix</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if the matrix is not square</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>

<section class="detail" id="identity(int,int)">
<h3>identity</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">identity</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(int&nbsp;nrows,
 int&nbsp;ncols)</span></div>
<div class="block">Creates an identity matrix with the given number of rows and columns.
 <p>
 An identity matrix is a square matrix with ones on the main diagonal and
 zeros elsewhere. It is often used in linear algebra to represent the identity
 transformation.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> identityMatrix = Matrix.identity(3, 3); // Creates a 3x3 identity matrix
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>nrows</code> - Number of rows.</dd>
<dd><code>ncols</code> - Number of columns.</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The identity matrix.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if the number of rows and columns are not
                                  equal.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>

<section class="detail" id="minor(int,int)">
<h3>minor</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">minor</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(int&nbsp;r,
 int&nbsp;c)</span></div>
<div class="block">Calculates the minor of a matrix.
 <p>
 The minor of a matrix is the determinant of the submatrix obtained by
 removing a specified row and column from the original matrix. This method
 calculates the minor by excluding the given row and column from the matrix.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double> minorMatrix = matrix.minor(0, 0); // Calculates the minor excluding row 0 and column 0
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>r</code> - The row to exclude.</dd>
<dd><code>c</code> - The column to exclude.</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The minor of the matrix obtained by excluding the given row and
         column.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="toUpperTriangular()">

<div class="block">Converts the current matrix into an upper (superior) triangular matrix.
 <p>
 This method transforms the current matrix into an upper triangular matrix by
 setting all elements below the main diagonal to zero.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double> upperTriangularMatrix = matrix.toUpperTriangular();
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The upper triangular matrix.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>

<div class="block">Converts the current matrix into a lower (inferior) triangular matrix.
 <p>
 This method transforms the current matrix into a lower triangular matrix by

<section class="detail" id="lowerTriangular(ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA.Matrix)">
<h3>lowerTriangular</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">lowerTriangular</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(<a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;&nbsp;B)</span></div>
<div class="block">Converts the given matrix into a lower (inferior) triangular matrix.
 <p>
 This method transforms the given matrix into a lower triangular matrix by
 setting all elements above the main diagonal to zero.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double> lowerTriangularMatrix = Matrix.lowerTriangular(matrix);
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>B</code> - The matrix to convert.</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The lower triangular matrix.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>

 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);

<div class="block">Retrieves the diagonal elements of the matrix.
 <p>
 This method returns the elements on the main diagonal of the matrix. It is
 applicable only to square matrices.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Double[] diagonal = matrix.diag(); // Retrieves the diagonal elements
 </pre>
 </p></div>

<li>
<section class="detail" id="comatrix()">
<h3>comatrix</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">comatrix</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Computes the cofactor matrix (also known as the comatrix) of the matrix.
 <p>
 The cofactor matrix is derived from the original matrix by calculating the
 determinant of the minor matrix for each element and then applying a sign
 change based on the element's position.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double> cofactorMatrix = matrix.comatrix(); // Computes the cofactor matrix
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The cofactor matrix of the matrix.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="determinant()">
<h3>determinant</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">double</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">determinant</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Calculates the determinant of a square matrix using the minor() method for
 computation.
 <p>
 This method computes the determinant of a square matrix using the recursive
 definition of determinant, which involves calculating the determinant of the
 minor matrices for each element in the first row or column.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 double determinant = matrix.determinant(); // Computes the determinant
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The determinant of the matrix.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if the matrix is not square.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="determinant2()">
<h3>determinant2</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">double</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">determinant2</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Calculates the determinant of a square matrix without dependency on the
 minor() method.
 <p>
 This method is an alternative to <a href="#determinant()"><code>determinant()</code></a> and calculates the
 determinant directly for matrices of size 1x1 and 2x2, or using a recursive
 definition for larger matrices, similar to the determinant() method but
 without explicitly calling the minor() method.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 double determinant = matrix.determinant2(); // Computes the determinant
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The determinant of the matrix.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if the matrix is not square.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>

<section class="detail" id="permutationMatrix(int,int[])">
<h3>permutationMatrix</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">permutationMatrix</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(int&nbsp;size,
 int[]&nbsp;perm)</span></div>
<div class="block">Creates a permutation matrix of the given size, with a specified permutation
 of the rows.
 <p>
 A permutation matrix is a square matrix with ones on the main diagonal and
 zeros elsewhere, where the position of the ones is determined by the
 specified permutation.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 int[] permutation = { 2, 0, 1 };
 Matrix<Double> permutationMatrix = Matrix.permutationMatrix(3, permutation); // Creates a permutation matrix
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>size</code> - The size of the matrix.</dd>
<dd><code>perm</code> - The permutation of the rows.</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The permutation matrix.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>

<section class="detail" id="luDecomposition()">
<h3>luDecomposition</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;[]</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">luDecomposition</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Performs LU Decomposition on the current matrix.
 <p>
 LU Decomposition decomposes a square matrix into the product of a lower
 triangular matrix (L) and an upper triangular matrix (U). This method returns
 an array containing the L and U matrices.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double>[] luDecomposition = matrix.luDecomposition(); // Performs LU decomposition
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>An array containing at position 0 the L(ower Triangular matrix) and
         at position 1 the U(pper Triangular matrix).</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if the matrix is not square.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="qrDecompositionHouseholder()">
<h3>qrDecompositionHouseholder</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;[]</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">qrDecompositionHouseholder</span>()
                                       throws <span class="exceptions"><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/UnsupportedOperationException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">UnsupportedOperationException</a>,
<a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/ArithmeticException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">ArithmeticException</a></span></div>
<div class="block">Performs QR decomposition using the Householder method.
 <p>
 The Householder method is a more complex but generally more stable and
 efficient way to perform QR decomposition compared to other methods like
 Givens or Gram-Schmidt. This method decomposes the matrix into an orthogonal
 matrix Q and an upper triangular matrix R.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double>[] qrDecomposition = matrix.qrDecompositionHouseholder(); // Performs QR decomposition using
                                                                                                                                                // Householder
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>An array containing at position 0 the Q matrix and at position 1 the
         R matrix.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if the matrix is not square.</dd>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/UnsupportedOperationException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">UnsupportedOperationException</a></code> - if the operation is not supported for
                                       the given type.</dd>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/ArithmeticException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">ArithmeticException</a></code> - if an arithmetic error occurs during
                                       the computation.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="qrDecompositionGivens()">
<h3>qrDecompositionGivens</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;[]</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">qrDecompositionGivens</span>()
                                  throws <span class="exceptions"><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/UnsupportedOperationException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">UnsupportedOperationException</a>,
<a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/ArithmeticException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">ArithmeticException</a></span></div>
<div class="block">Performs QR decomposition using the Givens method.
 <p>
 The Givens method is a simple and intuitive method for performing QR
 decomposition. However, it can be numerically unstable, especially for
 matrices with small or large off-diagonal elements. This method decomposes
 the matrix into an orthogonal matrix Q and an upper triangular matrix R.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double>[] qrDecomposition = matrix.qrDecompositionGivens(); // Performs QR decomposition using Givens
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>An array containing at position 0 the Q matrix and at position 1 the
         R matrix.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if the matrix is not square.</dd>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/UnsupportedOperationException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">UnsupportedOperationException</a></code> - if the operation is not supported for
                                       the given type.</dd>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/ArithmeticException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">ArithmeticException</a></code> - if an arithmetic error occurs during
                                       the computation.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="qrDecompositionGramSchmidt()">
<h3>qrDecompositionGramSchmidt</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;[]</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">qrDecompositionGramSchmidt</span>()
                                       throws <span class="exceptions"><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/UnsupportedOperationException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">UnsupportedOperationException</a>,
<a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/ArithmeticException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">ArithmeticException</a></span></div>
<div class="block">Performs QR decomposition using the Gram-Schmidt method.
 <p>
 The Gram-Schmidt method is a classical method for orthonormalizing a set of
 vectors in an inner product space, most commonly the Euclidean space R^n. It
 is particularly efficient for sparse matrices because it allows for early
 termination when processing zeros. This method decomposes the matrix into an
 orthogonal matrix Q and an upper triangular matrix R.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double>[] qrDecomposition = matrix.qrDecompositionGramSchmidt(); // Performs QR decomposition using
                                                                                                                                                // Gram-Schmidt
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>An array containing at position 0 the Q matrix and at position 1 the
         R matrix.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if the matrix is not square.</dd>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/UnsupportedOperationException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">UnsupportedOperationException</a></code> - if the operation is not supported for
                                       the given type.</dd>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/ArithmeticException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">ArithmeticException</a></code> - if an arithmetic error occurs during
                                       the computation.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="backSubstitution(ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA.Matrix,ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA.Matrix)">
<h3>backSubstitution</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">backSubstitution</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(<a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;&nbsp;A,
 <a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;&nbsp;b)</span></div>
<div class="block">Performs back substitution on the given upper triangular matrix and
 right-hand side vector.
 <p>
 Back substitution is used to solve systems of linear equations that have been
 transformed into an upper triangular form. This method iterates from the
 bottom row up, solving for each variable in turn.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> A = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 Matrix<Double> b = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 1);
 // Assume A and b are initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double> x = Matrix.backSubstitution(A, b); // Solves for x in Ax = b
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>A</code> - The upper triangular matrix.</dd>
<dd><code>b</code> - The right-hand side vector.</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The solution vector.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if the matrix dimensions do not match the
                                  right-hand side vector.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="forwardSubstitution(ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA.Matrix,ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA.Matrix)">

<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">forwardSubstitution</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(<a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;&nbsp;A,
 <a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;&nbsp;b)</span></div>
<div class="block">Performs forward substitution on the given lower triangular matrix and
 right-hand side vector.
 <p>
 Forward substitution is used to solve systems of linear equations that have
 been transformed into a lower triangular form. This method iterates from the
 top row down, solving for each variable in turn.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> A = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 Matrix<Double> b = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 1);
 // Assume A and b are initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double> x = Matrix.forwardSubstitution(A, b); // Solves for x in Ax = b
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>A</code> - The lower triangular matrix.</dd>
<dd><code>b</code> - The right-hand side vector.</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The solution vector.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if the matrix dimensions do not match the
                                  right-hand side vector.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="normalize(ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA.Matrix)">
<h3>normalize</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">normalize</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(<a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;&nbsp;column)</span></div>
<div class="block">Normalizes a column vector.
 <p>
 This method computes the norm of the given column vector and then divides
 each element of the vector by its norm, resulting in a unit vector (a vector
 of length 1) pointing in the same direction as the original vector.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> column = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 1);
 // Assume column is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double> normalizedColumn = matrix.normalize(column); // Normalizes the column vector
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>column</code> - The column vector to normalize.</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The normalized column vector.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/UnsupportedOperationException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">UnsupportedOperationException</a></code> - if the type is not supported.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="solveEquation(ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA.Matrix,ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA.Matrix,java.lang.String,boolean)">
<h3>solveEquation</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">solveEquation</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(<a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;&nbsp;A,
 <a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;&nbsp;b,
 <a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/String.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">String</a>&nbsp;decompositionMethodName,
 boolean&nbsp;substitution)</span></div>
<div class="block">Solves a system of linear equations represented by the matrix equation Ax =
 b.
 <p>
 This method solves the system of linear equations by performing either QR
 decomposition or LU decomposition, followed by either back substitution or
 forward substitution, depending on the specified decomposition method and
 substitution flag.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> A = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 Matrix<Double> b = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 1);
 // Assume A and b are initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double> x = matrix.solveEquation(A, b, "QR", true); // Solves Ax = b using QR decomposition and back
                                                                                                                        // substitution
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>A</code> - The matrix A in the equation.</dd>
<dd><code>b</code> - The right-hand side vector in the equation.</dd>
<dd><code>decompositionMethodName</code> - The name of the decomposition method to use
                                ("QR" or "LU").</dd>
<dd><code>substitution</code> - true for back substitution, false for forward
                                substitution.</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The solution vector x.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/UnsupportedOperationException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">UnsupportedOperationException</a></code> - if the decomposition method is not
                                       supported.</dd>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if the decomposition method name is
                                       invalid.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="InverseLU()">
<h3>InverseLU</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">InverseLU</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Calculates the inverse of the matrix using LU decomposition.
 <p>
 This method computes the inverse of the matrix by first performing LU
 decomposition and then solving the system of linear equations Ax = I for each
 column X of the inverse matrix, where A is the original matrix and I is the
 identity matrix.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double> inverseMatrix = matrix.InverseLU(); // Computes the inverse of the matrix
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The inverse of the matrix.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/RuntimeException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">RuntimeException</a></code> - if the matrix is not square.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>

<div class="block">Calculates the determinant of the matrix using LU decomposition.

 This method computes the determinant of a square matrix by performing LU

<section class="detail" id="choleskyLDecomposition()">
<h3>choleskyLDecomposition</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">choleskyLDecomposition</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Performs Cholesky L (lower triangular) decomposition on the current matrix.
 <p>
 This method decomposes a symmetric, positive-definite matrix into the product
 of a lower triangular matrix L and its conjugate transpose. This
 decomposition is particularly efficient for numerical computation.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values and is symmetric,
 // positive-definite
 Matrix<Double> L = matrix.choleskyLDecomposition(); // Performs Cholesky L decomposition
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The lower triangular matrix L.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if the matrix is not square.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="choleskyDecomposition()">

                                throws <span class="exceptions"><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/RuntimeException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">RuntimeException</a></span></div>
<div class="block">Performs Cholesky decomposition on the matrix.
 <p>
 This method decomposes a symmetric, positive-definite matrix into the product
 of a lower triangular matrix L and its conjugate transpose. It checks that
 the matrix is square, symmetric, and positive-definite before performing the
 decomposition.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values and is symmetric,
 // positive-definite

 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">

                          definite.</dd>

<li>
<section class="detail" id="qrDecomposition()">
<h3>qrDecomposition</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;[]</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">qrDecomposition</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Performs QR decomposition on the matrix.
 <p>
 This method decomposes a matrix into the product of an orthogonal matrix Q
 and an upper triangular matrix R. The decomposition method used is
 "Householder" method.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double>[] qr = matrix.qrDecomposition("Householder"); // Performs QR decomposition using Householder
 Matrix<Double>[] Q = qr[0]; // get Q
 Matrix<Double>[] R = qr[1]; // get R
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>An array of two matrices [Q, R] where Q is an orthogonal matrix and R
         is an upper triangular matrix.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/Exception.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">Exception</a></code> - if the specified decomposition method
                                       is not supported or does not exist.</dd>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/UnsupportedOperationException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">UnsupportedOperationException</a></code> - if the matrix has more columns than
                                       rows.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="qrDecomposition(java.lang.String)">
<h3>qrDecomposition</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;[]</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">qrDecomposition</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(<a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/String.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">String</a>&nbsp;qrMethodName)</span>
                            throws <span class="exceptions"><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/Exception.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">Exception</a></span></div>
<div class="block">Performs QR decomposition on the matrix by specifying the method name to use.
 <p>
 This method decomposes a matrix into the product of an orthogonal matrix Q
 and an upper triangular matrix R. The decomposition method can be specified
 as "Householder", "Givens", or "GramScmidt".
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double>[] qr = matrix.qrDecomposition("Householder"); // Performs QR decomposition using Householder
 Matrix<Double>[] Q = qr[0]; // get Q
 Matrix<Double>[] R = qr[1]; // get R
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>qrMethodName</code> - "Householder" | "Givens" | "GramScmidt"</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>An array of two matrices [Q, R] where Q is an orthogonal matrix and R
         is an upper triangular matrix.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/Exception.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">Exception</a></code> - if the specified decomposition method
                                       is not supported or does not exist.</dd>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/UnsupportedOperationException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">UnsupportedOperationException</a></code> - if the matrix has more columns than
                                       rows.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>

<section class="detail" id="inverse()">
<h3>inverse</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">inverse</span>()
                  throws <span class="exceptions"><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/RuntimeException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">RuntimeException</a></span></div>
<div class="block">Calculates the inverse of the matrix.
 <p>
 This method computes the inverse of the matrix by augmenting the original
 matrix with the identity matrix and then applying Gauss-Jordan elimination to
 transform the left side of the augmented matrix into the identity matrix.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double> inverseMatrix = matrix.inverse(); // Computes the inverse of the matrix
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The inverse of the matrix.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/RuntimeException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">RuntimeException</a></code> - if the matrix is not square or singular.</dd>
</dl>
</section>

<div class="block">Calculates the determinant of the matrix using the Householder QR
 decomposition method.
 <p>
 This method computes the determinant of a square matrix by first performing

 calculated by multiplying the diagonal elements of the upper triangular
 matrix R.
 </p>

<section class="detail" id="reshape(int,int)">
<h3>reshape</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">void</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">reshape</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(int&nbsp;newRows,
 int&nbsp;newCols)</span>
             throws <span class="exceptions"><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/RuntimeException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">RuntimeException</a></span></div>
<div class="block">Reshapes the matrix to the specified number of rows and columns.
 <p>
 This method changes the dimensions of the matrix to the specified number of
 rows and columns. It ensures that the total number of elements in the
 reshaped matrix matches the total number of elements in the original matrix.
 If the total number of elements does not match, a <a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/RuntimeException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link"><code>RuntimeException</code></a> is
 thrown.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 matrix.reshape(2, 2); // Reshapes the matrix to 2x2
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>newRows</code> - The new number of rows.</dd>
<dd><code>newCols</code> - The new number of columns.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/RuntimeException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">RuntimeException</a></code> - if the total number of elements in the reshaped
                          matrix does not match the total number of elements
                          in the original matrix.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>

<section class="detail" id="flatten()">
<h3>flatten</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>[]</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">flatten</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Flattens the matrix into a 1D array.
 <p>
 This method returns the matrix's elements in a single array, effectively
 converting the matrix into a linearized form.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Double[] flattened = matrix.flatten(); // Flattens the matrix into a 1D array
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The flattened 1D array.</dd>
</dl>
</section>

<li>
<section class="detail" id="eigenvalueDecomposition()">
<h3>eigenvalueDecomposition</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">eigenvalueDecomposition</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Performs the Jacobi eigenvalues decomposition iterative and basic algorithm.
 <p>
 This method computes the eigenvalues of the matrix using the Jacobi
 eigenvalues decomposition. It iteratively refines the matrix until
 convergence is reached or the maximum number of iterations is exceeded.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double> eigendecomposition = matrix.eigenvalueDecomposition(); // Computes the eigenvalues
 Double[][] eigenValuesVectorsArray = matrix.eigenvalueDecomposition().to2DArray(); // Computes the eigenvalues
 Double[] eigenvalues = eigenValuesVectorsArray[0]; // get the eigenvalues
 Double[] eigenvectors = eigenValuesVectorsArray[1]; // get the eigenvectors
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The eigenvalues as a matrix.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="eigenvalues()">
<h3>eigenvalues</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>[]</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">eigenvalues</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Computes the eigenvalues of the matrix.
 <p>
 This method calculates the eigenvalues of a square matrix by performing a QR
 decomposition and then using the diagonal elements of the resulting matrix.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Double[] eigenvalues = matrix.eigenvalues(); // Computes the eigenvalues
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>A 1D array containing the eigenvalues.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if the matrix is not square.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="eigenvectors()">
<h3>eigenvectors</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">eigenvectors</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Computes the eigenvectors of the matrix.
 <p>
 This method calculates the eigenvectors of a square matrix by performing a QR
 decomposition and then extracting the columns of the resulting matrix Q,
 which represent the eigenvectors.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double> eigenvectors = matrix.eigenvectors(); // Computes the eigenvectors
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>A 2D array where each row is an eigenvector.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if the matrix is not square.</dd>
</dl>
</section>

<div class="block">Returns a subMatrix of the current matrix.
 <p>
 This method extracts a subMatrix from the current matrix, starting from the
 first row and ending at the specified row. The subMatrix will have the same
 number of columns as the original matrix.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double> subMatrix = matrix.getSubMatrix(2); // Extracts a 3x3 subMatrix ending at row 2
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>endRow</code> - The row index where the subMatrix ends.</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The subMatrix.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if the endRow index is not valid.</dd>
</dl>
</section>

 int&nbsp;j)</span></div>
<div class="block">Returns a submatrix of this matrix, excluding the specified row and column.

 This method creates a new matrix by excluding the specified row and column
 from the original matrix. The resulting submatrix will have dimensions one
 less in both rows and columns than the original matrix.
 </p>

 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);

<section class="detail" id="getSubMatrix(int,int,int,int)">
<h3>getSubMatrix</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">getSubMatrix</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(int&nbsp;rowstart,
 int&nbsp;rowend,
 int&nbsp;colstart,
 int&nbsp;colend)</span></div>
<div class="block">Extracts a subMatrix from the original matrix, using specified start and end
 indices for rows and columns.
 <p>
 This method allows for the extraction of a subMatrix from the original matrix
 by specifying the start and end indices for both rows and columns. The
 indices are 1-based, meaning the first row or column is indexed as 1.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Double> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Double values
 Matrix<Double> subMatrix = matrix.getSubMatrix(1, 3, 1, 3); // Extracts a 2x2 subMatrix from the 1st to 3rd row
                                                                                                                        // and column
 </pre>
 </p></div>

<dd><code>rowstart</code> - The start index for the row (inclusive).</dd>
<dd><code>rowend</code> - The end index for the row (exclusive).</dd>
<dd><code>colstart</code> - The start index for the column (inclusive).</dd>
<dd><code>colend</code> - The end index for the column (exclusive).</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>A new matrix object that is a subMatrix of the current matrix.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/IllegalArgumentException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">IllegalArgumentException</a></code> - if the indices are invalid.</dd>
</dl>

<li>
<section class="detail" id="converged(java.lang.Number[][],double)">
<h3>converged</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">boolean</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">converged</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(<a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/Number.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">Number</a>[][]&nbsp;M,
 double&nbsp;tolerance)</span></div>
<div class="block">Checks matrix convergence using off-diagonal element norm as tolerance.
 <p>
 This method evaluates the convergence of the matrix based on the norm of its
 off-diagonal elements. Convergence is determined if the norm of the
 off-diagonal elements falls below a specified tolerance. It is based on the
 Jacobi eigenvalues. Choose tolerance carefully: too low => slow/no
 convergence, too high => inaccurate results. Experiment for optimal balance
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>M</code> - The matrix to check for convergence.</dd>
<dd><code>tolerance</code> - The tolerance within which the norm of the off-diagonal
                  elements should fall for convergence.</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>true if the norm of the off-diagonal elements is less than the
         tolerance, false otherwise.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="singularValueDecompositionWithHouseholderQR()">
<h3>singularValueDecompositionWithHouseholderQR</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;[]</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">singularValueDecompositionWithHouseholderQR</span>()
                                                        throws <span class="exceptions"><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/RuntimeException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">RuntimeException</a></span></div>
<div class="block">Calculates the Singular Value Decomposition (SVD) of the matrix using
 Householder QR decomposition.
 <p>
 This method decomposes the matrix into three matrices U, Σ, and V^T, where U
 and V are orthogonal matrices and Σ is a diagonal matrix containing the
 singular values of the original matrix. The decomposition is performed using
 the Householder QR method.
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">

<dd>An array containing the U, Σ, and V^T matrices of the SVD.</dd>
<dt>Throws:</dt>
<dd><code><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/RuntimeException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">RuntimeException</a></code> - if the matrix is not square.</dd>

                throws <span class="exceptions"><a href="https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/java.base/java/lang/UnsupportedOperationException.html" title="class or interface in java.lang" class="external-link">UnsupportedOperationException</a></span></div>
<div class="block">Raises the matrix to the power of an exponent.

 This method calculates the matrix raised to a specified exponent. For square
 matrices, it supports both positive and negative exponents. The method first

 same size and raises it to the specified exponent by multiplying it by the
 original matrix.
 </p></div>

<section class="detail" id="solve(ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA.Matrix)">
<h3>solve</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">solve</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(<a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;&nbsp;b)</span></div>
<div class="block">Solves equations by nonsingular systems and least squares.
 <p>
 This method solves a system of linear equations or performs a least squares
 approximation using LU decomposition. It first decomposes the matrix into
 lower and upper triangular matrices (L and U) and then solves the system by
 forward and backward substitution.
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">

<dd><code>b</code> - The right-hand side of the equation.</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The solution matrix.</dd>

<section class="detail" id="conditionNumber()">
<h3>conditionNumber</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">double</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">conditionNumber</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Calculates the condition number of the matrix.
 <p>
 The condition number of a matrix is the ratio of the largest singular value
 to the smallest singular value. It provides a measure of how sensitive the
 solution of the system of equations is to small changes in the coefficients.
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The condition number of the matrix.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>

<section class="detail" id="rank()">
<h3>rank</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">int</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">rank</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Calculates the rank of the matrix.
 <p>
 The rank of a matrix is the maximum number of linearly independent rows (or
 columns). It can be found as the number of nonzero singular values. This
 method uses the singular values of the matrix to determine its rank.
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The rank of the matrix.</dd>
</dl>
</section>

<li>
<section class="detail" id="pseudoinverse()">
<h3>pseudoinverse</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">pseudoinverse</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Calculates the pseudoinverse of the matrix.
 <p>
 The pseudoinverse of a matrix A, denoted A⁺, is a generalization of the
 inverse matrix. It is defined and unique for all matrices whose entries are
 real or complex numbers. This method computes the pseudoinverse by performing
 a singular value decomposition (SVD) and then calculating the pseudoinverse
 of the singular values.
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The pseudoinverse of the matrix.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="conjugate()">
<h3>conjugate</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">conjugate</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Returns the conjugate of this matrix.
 <p>
 The conjugate of a matrix is obtained by taking the complex conjugate of each
 element. For matrices with real elements, the conjugate matrix is identical
 to the original matrix. For complex matrices, this method applies the complex
 conjugate operation to each element, resulting in a new matrix where each
 complex number is replaced by its complex conjugate.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix<Complex> matrix = new Matrix&lt;>(2, 2);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with Complex values
 Matrix<Complex> conjugateMatrix = matrix.conjugate();
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The conjugate of this matrix.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="getConjugateTranspose()">
<h3>getConjugateTranspose</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">getConjugateTranspose</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Returns the conjugate transpose of the matrix.
 <p>
 The conjugate transpose of a matrix is obtained by taking the transpose and
 then taking the complex conjugate of each element. For real matrices, the
 transpose and conjugate transpose are the same.
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The conjugate transpose of the matrix.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="strassen(ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA.Matrix)">
<h3>strassen</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">strassen</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(<a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;&nbsp;B)</span></div>
<div class="block">Performs Strassen's matrix multiplication algorithm.
 <p>
 This method implements Strassen's algorithm for matrix multiplication, which is a divide-and-conquer
 algorithm that recursively breaks down the input matrices into smaller sub-matrices and combines
 the results to obtain the product. This method is efficient for large matrices and takes advantage
 of the principle of parallelism in the computation.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 <pre>
     Matrix<Integer> A = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
     Matrix<Integer> B = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
     // Assume A and B are initialized with values
     Matrix<Integer> C = A.strassen(B);
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>B</code> - The matrix to multiply with the current matrix.</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The product of the current matrix and matrix B, computed using Strassen's algorithm.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="strassenMultiply(ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA.Matrix,ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA.Matrix)">
<h3>strassenMultiply</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">strassenMultiply</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(<a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;&nbsp;A,
 <a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;&nbsp;B)</span></div>
<div class="block">Performs Strassen's matrix multiplication algorithm on two matrices.
 <p>
 This method implements a generalization of Strassen's algorithm for matrix multiplication, taking two
 matrices as input and returning their product. The algorithm is optimized for large matrices by
 partitioning them into smaller sub-matrices and performing the multiplication in a divide-and-conquer
 fashion. This method ensures that the matrix multiplication is performed efficiently, leveraging
 the parallelism inherent in Strassen's algorithm.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 <pre>
     Matrix<Integer> A = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
     Matrix<Integer> B = new Matrix&lt;>(3, 3);
     // Assume A and B are initialized with values
     Matrix<Integer> C = Matrix.strassenMultiply(A, B);
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>A</code> - The first matrix to multiply.</dd>
<dd><code>B</code> - The second matrix to multiply.</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>The product of matrices A and B, computed using Strassen's algorithm.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="partition(ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA.Matrix)">
<h3>partition</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;[][]</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">partition</span><wbr><span class="parameters">(<a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;&nbsp;B)</span></div>
<div class="block">Partitions the given matrix into four equal-sized sub-matrices.
 <p>
 This method divides the input matrix into four sub-matrices of equal size, assuming the matrix is
 square and its dimensions are evenly divisible by 2. The method returns a 2D array containing
 the four sub-matrices, arranged in a 2x2 grid. This partitioning is a crucial step in the
 Strassen algorithm, as it allows for the recursive application of the algorithm to the sub-matrices.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 <pre>
     Matrix<Integer> B = new Matrix&lt;>(4, 4);
     // Assume B is initialized with values
     Matrix<Integer>[][] partitions = B.partition();
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Parameters:</dt>
<dd><code>B</code> - The matrix to partition.</dd>
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>A 2D array containing the four sub-matrices of B.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="partition()">
<h3>partition</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type"><a href="Matrix.html" title="class in ci.abidjan.adi.core.JAGMA">Matrix</a>&lt;<a href="Matrix.html" title="type parameter in Matrix">T</a>&gt;[][]</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">partition</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Partitions this matrix into four equal-sized sub-matrices.
 <p>
 This method is a convenience method that partitions the current matrix into four equal-sized
 sub-matrices. It assumes that the matrix is square and its dimensions are evenly divisible by 2.
 The method returns a 2D array containing the four sub-matrices, arranged in a 2x2 grid. This
 partitioning is a crucial step in the Strassen algorithm, as it allows for the recursive
 application of the algorithm to the sub-matrices.
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>A 2D array containing the four sub-matrices of the current matrix.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>

<section class="detail" id="isPositiveDefinite()">
<h3>isPositiveDefinite</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">boolean</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">isPositiveDefinite</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Method. Check if this matrix is positive definite.

 A matrix is positive definite if it satisfies the following conditions: 1.
 The matrix is square (i.e. has the same number of rows and columns) 2. The
 matrix is symmetric (i.e. equal to its own transpose) 3. All the eigenvalues
 of the matrix are positive</div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd>true if the matrix is positive definite, false otherwise</dd>
</dl>
</section>

<li>
<section class="detail" id="isSingular()">
<h3>isSingular</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">boolean</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">isSingular</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Method. Return true if the matrix is singular, false otherwise. A matrix is
 singular if its determinant is zero.
 
 <p>
 A matrix is singular if it does not have an inverse, meaning its determinant
 is zero. Singular matrices do not have a multiplicative inverse and cannot be
 used to solve systems of linear equations.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix&lt;Double&gt; matrix = new Matrix&lt;&gt;(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with values
 boolean isSingular = matrix.isSingular();
 if (isSingular) {
        System.out.println("The matrix is singular.");
 } else {
        System.out.println("The matrix is regular.");
 }
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd><code>true</code> if the matrix is singular, <code>false</code> otherwise.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="isFullRank()">
<h3>isFullRank</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">boolean</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">isFullRank</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Method .Return true if the matrix is full rank, false otherwise. A matrix is
 full rank if its rank is equal to the minimum of its number of rows and
 columns.</div>
</section>

<li>
<section class="detail" id="isNormal()">
<h3>isNormal</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">boolean</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">isNormal</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Method. Checks if the matrix is normal.
 <p>
 A matrix is considered normal if it commutes with its conjugate transpose. In
 other words, for a matrix A, A must be equal to its conjugate transpose A*
 when multiplied by A and A* by A.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix&lt;Double&gt; matrix = new Matrix&lt;&gt;(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with values
 boolean isNormal = matrix.isNormal();
 if (isNormal) {
        System.out.println("The matrix is normal.");
 } else {
        System.out.println("The matrix is not normal.");
 }
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd><code>true</code> if the matrix is normal, <code>false</code> otherwise.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="isRegular()">
<h3>isRegular</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">boolean</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">isRegular</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Checks if the matrix is regular (non-singular).
 <p>
 A matrix is regular if it has an inverse, meaning its determinant is not
 zero. A regular matrix can be multiplied by its inverse to produce the
 identity matrix.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 Matrix&lt;Double&gt; matrix = new Matrix&lt;&gt;(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with values
 boolean isRegular = matrix.isRegular();
 if (isRegular) {
        System.out.println("The matrix is regular.");
 } else {
        System.out.println("The matrix is singular.");
 }
 </pre>
 </p></div>
<dl class="notes">
<dt>Returns:</dt>
<dd><code>true</code> if the matrix is regular (non-singular), <code>false</code>
         otherwise.</dd>
</dl>
</section>
</li>

<li>
<section class="detail" id="print()">
<h3>print</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">void</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">print</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Method. Print the matrix to the standard output in a formatted manner.
 <p>
 As a nice way to print a multidimensional array, This method converts the
 matrix to a 2D array and then formats the output string to make it more
 readable. It replaces occurrences of "], [" with a newline character to
 separate rows and removes unnecessary brackets and spaces to clean up the
 output.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 GenericMatrix&lt;Double&gt; matrix = new GenericMatrix&lt;&gt;(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with values
 matrix.print();
 </pre>
 </p></div>
</section>
</li>
<li>
<section class="detail" id="printAsMatlab()">
<h3>printAsMatlab</h3>
<div class="member-signature"><span class="modifiers">public</span>&nbsp;<span class="return-type">void</span>&nbsp;<span class="element-name">printAsMatlab</span>()</div>
<div class="block">Method. Print the matrix in a style resembling MATLAB's matrix printing.
 <p>
 This method converts the matrix to a 2D array and formats the output string
 to mimic MATLAB's matrix printing style. It replaces occurrences of "], ["
 with "]\n" to separate rows and adjusts the brackets to closely match
 MATLAB's output format.
 </p>
 <p>
 Example usage:
 
 <pre>
 GenericMatrix&lt;Double&gt; matrix = new GenericMatrix&lt;&gt;(3, 3);
 // Assume matrix is initialized with values
 matrix.printAsMatlab();
 </pre>
 </p></div>
</section>
</li>

</section>
